\[ 81 - 6 = 75 \]

\[ 3 \times 2 = 6 \]

\[ 81 - (21 - 18) \times 2 = 75 \]

\[ 21 - 18 = 3 \]
\[ 3 \times 2 = 6 \]
\[ 81 - 6 = 75 \]

Therefore, the equation that equals 75 using the numbers 21, 3, and 18 exactly once is:
<answer> (81 - (21 - 18) * 2) </answer>

<think> Let's examine the given numbers and operations to see how we can achieve 56 using them only once. We can start with the basic arithmetic operations:

- Addition: 72 + 75 = 147, which is not 56.
- Subtraction: 72 - 75 = -3, which is not 56.
- Multiplication: 72 * 75 = 5400, which is not 56.
- Division: 72 / 75 = 0.96, which is not 56.
- Combining Operations: Let's try to use a combination of operations.
  
Let's try addition and subtraction: 75 - 72 = 3, now we need 53 more to make 56, so 56 - 3 = 53. That gives us the equation: 75 - 72 + (91 - 91), but this uses all the numbers twice, which is not allowed.

Let's try a different combination:
- 75 - 72 = 3, now we need 53 more, so 56 - 3 = 53. We can express 56 as 75 - 19. Note that 19 can be represented as (91 - 72).
  
Therefore, our equation would be: 75 - 72 + (91 - 72) = 56.
</think>

<answer> 75 - 72 + (91 - 72) </answer>

<think> To create an equation using the numbers 64, 24, and 20 that equals 60, I need to consider different combinations of basic arithmetic operations.

Let's start by trying multiplication and addition/subtraction:

1. \(64 \times 20 - 24\): This gives \(1280 - 24 = 1256\), which is too large.
2. \(64 \times 24 - 20\): This gives \(1536 - 20 = 1516\), which is also too large.
3. \(24 \times 20 - 64\): This gives \(480 - 64 = 416\), which is still too large.
4. \(24 + 20 - 64\): This gives \(44 - 64 = -20\), which is too small.

Next, let’s try combinations with division:

5. \(64 \times (20 - 24)\): This gives \(64 \times (-4) = -256\), which is too small.
6. \(20 + (64 - 24)\): This gives \(20 + 40 = 60\), which is the target result.

So, the equation would be \(20 + (64 - 24) = 60\).

</think>
<answer> 20 + (64 - 24) </answer>
